TITLE      Photoneutron reaction cross  sections  in  experiments M0635  1    3 
            with   beams   of   quasimonoenergetic   annihilation M0635  1    4 
            photons.                                              M0635  1    5 
AUTHOR     (V.V.Varlamov,N.N.Peskov,D.S.Rudenko,M.E.Stepanov)     M0635  1    6 
REFERENCE  (J,YK,,(1-2),48,2003)                                  M0635  1    7 
           (R,MSU-INP-2003-2/715,2003)                            M0635  1    8 
           (R,INDC(CCP)-440,37,2004)                              M0635  1    9 
INSTITUTE  (4RUSMOS)                                              M0635  1   10 
INC-SOURCE (QMPH,ARAD)                                            M0635  1   11 
ANALYSIS   The typical  differences  between Saclay and Livermore M0635  1   12 
            data are the following at the same time:              M0635  1   13 
            - as  a rule total photoneutron reaction (g,xn) cross M0635  1   14 
              section values (both amplitude and integrated cross M0635  1   15 
              section  values) obtained  at Livermore are smaller M0635  1   16 
              and  must  be  multiplied  by  special  coefficient M0635  1   17 
              (about 5 - 15%);                                    M0635  1   18 
            - the  (g,n) reaction (in fact - the sum of reactions M0635  1   19 
              (g,n) + (g,np))  cross section differ both in shape M0635  1   20 
              and magnitude,   these   of  Livermore  being  much M0635  1   21 
              smaller;                                            M0635  1   22 
            - the  (g,2n)  reaction  cross section differ both in M0635  1   23 
              shape and magnitude,  these of Livermore being much M0635  1   24 
              bigger.                                             M0635  1   25 
            Because two  laboratories  data  for  (g,xn) reaction M0635  1   26 
            cross section obtained without  neutron  multiplicity M0635  1   27 
            sorting  for  all gamma  energies disagree each other M0635  1   28 
            by about several percents,  but data  for  (g,n)  and M0635  1   29 
            (g,2n)  obtained  using neutron multiplicity sorting, M0635  1   30 
            disagree much more and in opposite sides  (while  the M0635  1   31 
            integrated (g,n) cross sections form Saclay are about M0635  1   32 
            40 % bigger than the Livermore data, their integrated M0635  1   33 
            (g,2n)   reaction  cross  sections  are  about  50  % M0635  1   34 
            smaller) on the base that Saclay neutron multiplicity M0635  1   35 
            sorting  procedure was not correct,  the Saclay (g,n) M0635  1   36 
            and (g,2n) reaction cross section data were modified. M0635  1   37 
            The equation                                          M0635  1   38 
             sig-2n-S-mod = sig-2n-S + 1/2*(sig-n-S - R*sig-n-L)  M0635  1   39 
            gives to  one  the  possibility to obtained evaluated M0635  1   40 
            (corrected, modified) Saclay cross  section  data  by M0635  1   41 
            transmitting  back  into  the  (g,2n)  reaction cross M0635  1   42 
            section  part  of  (g,n)   reaction   cross   section M0635  1   43 
            incorrectly putted  into  this channel.  The constant M0635  1   44 
            values R using for each investigated nucleus  in  the M0635  1   45 
            modification   formula   were   obtained   as  ratios M0635  1   46 
            (sig-xn-S)/(sig-xn-L) for total photoneutron reaction M0635  1   47 
            (g,xn)  cross  section  data  obtained  at Saclay and M0635  1   48 
            Livermore (in good agreement with previously  founded M0635  1   49 
            for big systematics value R-syst = 1.122 (0.243)).    M0635  1   50 
            Because the  evaluated  (corrected)   Saclay   (g,2n) M0635  1   51 
            reaction  cross  section  was  obtained  by  addition M0635  1   52 
            (moving back) the  "false"  part  of  (g,n)  reaction M0635  1   53 
            cross section                                         M0635  1   54 
                            1/2*(sig-n-S - r*sig-n-L)             M0635  1   55 
            the evaluated (corrected) Saclay (g,n) reaction cross M0635  1   56 
            section was obtained by subtraction of  that  "false" M0635  1   57 
            part                                                  M0635  1   58 
                sig-n-S-mod =  sig-n-S  -  (sig-n-S - r*sig-n-L), M0635  1   59 
            where part in brackets is calculating in the range of M0635  1   60 
            energies more  than  (g,2n) reaction threshold,  from M0635  1   61 
            correspondent (g,n) reaction cross  section  obtained M0635  1   62 
            at Saclay.                                            M0635  1   63 
            At the  same  time  Livermore  evaluated data for all M0635  1   64 
            three kinds of reactions ((g,xn), (g,n),  and (g,2n)) M0635  1   65 
            were obtained by multiplication by coefficient R.     M0635  1   66 
REL-REF    (E,,E.Wolinec+,J,RBF,17,56,1987) method for correction M0635  1   67 
            of (g,n)  and  (g,2n)  reaction  cross  section  data M0635  1   68 
            caused by   the   difference  in  the  analysis  that M0635  1   69 
            separates the total counts of neutrons into (g,n) and M0635  1   70 
            (g,2n) events.                                        M0635  1   71 
ERR-ANALYS (DATA-ERR) Mean-root-square uncertainties.             M0635  1   72 
COMMENT    The accurate system analysis of the (g,xn),  (g,n) and M0635  1   73 
            (g,2n)  reaction cross section data obtained by using M0635  1   74 
            quasimonoenergetical  annihilation  photon  beems  at M0635  1   75 
            Livermore  (USA)  and Saclay (France) was carried out M0635  1   76 
            for 19 (for 7 - at  first)  nuclei  51V,  75As,  89Y, M0635  1   77 
            90Zr,   115In,  116,117,118,120,124Sn,  127I,  133Cs, M0635  1   78 
            159Tb,  165Ho,  181Ta,  197Au, 208Pb, 232Th, 238U. It M0635  1   79 
            was  observed  that the (g,xn) reaction cross section M0635  1   80 
            data obtained  at  both  laboratories  without  using M0635  1   81 
            neutron multiplicity sorting procedure disagree by 10 M0635  1   82 
            - 15 %.  Additionally  it  was  found  out  that  the M0635  1   83 
            disagreement  of  partial  reactions (g,n) and (g,2n) M0635  1   84 
            cross sections,  obtained at both laboratories  using M0635  1   85 
            neutron    multiplicity    sorting    procedure   are M0635  1   86 
            significantly more (till 30 - 40 %)  and  as  a  rule M0635  1   87 
            have  opposite  directions.  These disagreements were M0635  1   88 
            interpreted as the result of  difference  of  neutron M0635  1   89 
            multiplicity   sorting   procedures   used   in  both M0635  1   90 
            laboratories:  that is incorrect at Saclay  with  the M0635  1   91 
            result  of  uncorrect  transmission  of  the  part of M0635  1   92 
            (g,2n) reaction cross section into the (g,n) reaction M0635  1   93 
            cross  section.  The  special method was used to move M0635  1   94 
            the  data  into  consistence.  Its   idea   is   that M0635  1   95 
            correspondent  "false"  part  of (g,n) reaction cross M0635  1   96 
            section is recalculated  and  transmitted  back  into M0635  1   97 
            (g,2n)  reaction  cross  section.  For  all 19 nuclei M0635  1   98 
            listed the jointly corrected (g,xn), (g,n) and (g,2n) M0635  1   99 
            reaction  cross  sections were evaluated and prepared M0635  1  100 
            for  including  into  the  EXFOR   nuclear   reaction M0635  1  101 
            database.                                             M0635  1  102
